There is no atomic update/replace operation, which creates a data-loss window: if an agent calls `memory_forget` and then `memory_store` in sequence and the store fails, the original memory is gone with nothing to replace it.\\n\\nAdditionally, there is no way to preview similar memories before storing, so agents can\\u0026#39;t detect conflicts before overwriting.\\n\\n## Solution\\n\\nThis PR adds a **`memory_refresh` tool** that operates in two modes:\\n\\n### Mode 1 — Search-only (no `memoryId`)\\n\\nCall with only `text` to preview similar memories before committing:\\n- Embeds `text` using the same model as `memory_recall`\\n- Searches LanceDB for top 3 similar entries (with cosine similarity scores)\\n- Returns matches **without storing anything**\\n- Agent reviews and decides whether to call again with a `memoryId` to replace\\n\\n```json\\n{ \\u0026#34;operation\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;search_only\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;matches\\u0026#34;: [{ \\u0026#34;id\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;text\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;category\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;importance\\u0026#34;: 0.8, \\u0026#34;similarity\\u0026#34;: 0.93 }] }\\n```\\n\\n### Mode 2 — Atomic replace (`memoryId` provided)\\n\\nAtomically replaces a specific memory:\\n1. Reads the existing entry (captures old text for audit)\\n2. Deletes the old entry\\n3. Inserts the new entry with `text`/`category`/`importance`\\n4. On insert failure: **best-effort rollback** restores the original (returns `rollbackWarning` in result)\\n5. Appends to audit log at `~/.openclaw/memory/refresh-audit.jsonl`\\n\\n```json\\n{ \\u0026#34;operation\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;replaced\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;old_id\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;new_id\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;old_text_preview\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;first 80 chars\\u0026#34; }\\n```\\n\\n### Audit log\\n\\nEvery Mode 2 operation appends a JSONL line to `~/.openclaw/memory/refresh-audit.jsonl` (created if absent):\\n\\n```json\\n{\\u0026#34;ts\\u0026#34;: 1234567890, \\u0026#34;operation\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;replaced\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;old_id\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;new_id\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;...\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;similarity\\u0026#34;: 0.95, \\u0026#34;old_text\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;first 80 chars\\u0026#34;, \\u0026#34;new_text\\u0026#34;: \\u0026#34;first 80 chars\\u0026#34;}\\n```\\n\\nNo audit entry is written for Mode 1 (search-only).\\n\\n## Changes\\n\\n- **`extensions/memory-lancedb/index.ts`**\\n  - Added `node:fs/promises`, `node:os`, `node:path` imports\\n  - Added `MemoryDB.getById(id)` using LanceDB filter query (`table.query().where(...).toArray()`)\\n  - Registered `memory_refresh` tool following the exact same pattern as the other three tools\\n\\n- **`extensions/memory-lancedb/index.test.ts`**\\n  - Updated live test tool count: 3 → 4\\n  - Added 4 unit tests (all mocked, no OpenAI key required):\\n    1. Search-only mode: returns top 3 matches with similarity, does NOT call `add`/`delete`\\n    2. Atomic replace: old entry deleted, new entry added, audit log written\\n    3. Non-existent `memoryId`: returns `error: not_found`, nothing written or deleted\\n    4. Best-effort rollback: when `add` fails, original is restored via second `add` call\\n\\n## Test results\\n\\n```\\n✓ extensions/memory-lancedb/index.test.ts (17 tests | 1 skipped) 123ms\\n  16 passed | 1 skipped (live test — needs OPENAI_API_KEY)\\n```\\n\\n## Related\\n\\nComplementary to #21003 (`memory_write`/upsert for file-based memory) — that PR covers the markdown/file memory system; this PR covers the LanceDB vector memory system. This issue was previously reported in #27419 and partially addressed, but the root cause — `onReplyStart` unconditionally resetting the typing breaker on every streaming chunk (`typing.ts:71-85`) — was not fixed, causing the problem to persist in later versions (confirmed on 2026.3.12+ with proxy configurations). The result is a cascade: streaming chunks repeatedly reset the typing circuit breaker, flooding the network with failing `sendChatAction` requests for 30s+, while the polling stall watchdog takes 90s to detect the outage. Meanwhile, outbound `sendMessage`/`editMessageText` calls fail silently with no retry.\\n- **Why it matters:** Users behind proxies lose AI replies entirely during transient network disruptions.\\n- **What changed:**\\n  1. **Typing guard semantics** — `onReplyStart` now only resets the breaker on the first call per reply cycle; subsequent streaming chunks refresh the TTL but never restart an already-tripped breaker\\n  2. **Outbound network health signal** — `sendChatAction` handler tracks consecutive recoverable network failures and triggers early polling restart (instead of waiting 90s)\\n  3. **Pre-connect send retry** — final replies, preview edits, text fallbacks, and user-visible error messages all retry on safe pre-connect network errors (connection refused, DNS, socket hang up) with exponential backoff\\n  4. **Configurable stall threshold** — new optional `channels.telegram.network.pollStallThresholdMs` lets proxy users lower the watchdog from the 90s default\\n  5. **Watchdog false positive fix** — polling stall detection now checks `runner.size()` to avoid false restarts when updates are still being processed (backpressure)\\n- **What did NOT change (scope boundary):** No transport fallback bypass for explicit proxies — respects user network policy. No changes to `reply-dispatcher.ts` error handling or general retry infrastructure.\\n\\n## Change Type (select all)\\n\\n- [x] Bug fix\\n\\n## Scope (select all touched areas)\\n\\n- [x] Integrations\\n\\n## Linked Issue/PR\\n\\n- Closes #27419\\n\\n## User-visible / Behavior Changes\\n\\n- Typing indicator no longer spams failing requests during network outages (was: 30s+ of error log flooding)\\n- Telegram replies now retry on safe pre-connect network errors instead of silently failing\\n- Polling recovery is faster when outbound sends detect network failure (seconds vs 90s)\\n- New optional config: `channels.telegram.network.pollStallThresholdMs` (default: 90000)\\n\\n## Security Impact (required)\\n\\n- New permissions/capabilities? Log transports registered by the diagnostics-otel plugin silently never attach to the real logger, so no OTLP log records are emitted. This PR moves the transport registry and the active logger reference to a `globalThis.__openclawLogTransportState` singleton, mirroring the existing pattern used by `__openclawDiagnosticEventsState` in `diagnostic-events.ts`.\\n\\n2. **Add opt-in content capture for OTEL traces** — Adds a `diagnostics.otel.includeContent` config flag (default: `false`) that gates attaching user-facing input/output text to `model.usage` trace spans. When enabled, content is emitted as standard `gen_ai.prompt` / `gen_ai.completion` attributes (primary), with `langfuse.observation.input` / `langfuse.observation.output` as secondary compatibility fields. All content is redacted via `redactSensitiveText` before export.\\n\\n## Why one PR\\n\\nThese are two independent fixes that happen to be small enough to review together (+86/-6 across 8 files). Without a shared `activeLogger`, `registerLogTransport` reads `loggingState.cachedLogger` which is `null` in the plugin\\u0026#39;s module instance, so the transport silently never attaches.\\n\\n**Content capture — compared with #36231, #21290, #40254:**\\n\\n- Smaller and more focused than #21290 (5735 lines, 40 files) — this PR takes the incremental approach of extending the existing `model.usage` flow rather than redesigning the span hierarchy\\n- Uses standard `gen_ai.*` attributes as the primary content fields (unlike #36231 which uses Langfuse-specific attrs as primary)\\n- Includes Langfuse compatibility attrs as secondary fields (unlike #21290 which only uses standard attrs)\\n- Does not include unrelated files like `PATCHES.md` (present in #36231)\\n- Covers the same emission site as #36231 (`agent-runner.ts`) with the same gating approach (`cfg.diagnostics?.otel?.includeContent`)\\n\\n### Scope note\\n\\nContent capture in this PR is at the reply layer (`agent-runner.ts`), capturing user-facing input/output text — not raw provider request/response bodies, reasoning internals, or tool call content. When compaction aborts and retries, the counter increments but the session context stays the same, causing the same content to be flushed repeatedly (4-7x duplicate entries reported).\\n\\nRoot cause: `compactionCount` conflates \\u0026#34;compaction cycle count\\u0026#34; with \\u0026#34;content has changed\\u0026#34; — these are independent concerns. Two different compaction cycles can see identical context (abort → retry scenario), so event-based dedup is fundamentally wrong for this use case.\\n\\n## How\\n- **State-based dedup**: compute a SHA-256 hash (truncated to 16 hex chars) of `messages.length + last 3 user/assistant message contents` before each flush. If the hash matches the stored `memoryFlushContextHash`, skip the flush.\\n- **Two-layer design**: `shouldRunMemoryFlush()` unchanged (token threshold gate), hash check added as second gate in `runMemoryFlushIfNeeded()`.\\n- **`willRetry` fix**: `onAgentEvent` now checks `!evt.data?.willRetry` before marking `memoryCompactionCompleted = true`, preventing retry-in-progress compaction from being incorrectly treated as completed.\\n- **Performance**: `readTranscriptTailMessages()` reads only the last 64KB of the transcript file (not the full file).\\n- **Hash timing**: stores the hash computed *before* the flush run (not after), since the flush turn itself writes to the transcript and would change the hash.\\n\\n### Scenario behavior\\n| Scenario | Behavior |\\n|----------|----------|\\n| Compaction abort | messages unchanged → hash unchanged → skip ✅ |\\n| Compaction success | messages compressed → hash changed → allow flush ✅ |\\n| New messages | tail content changed → hash changed → allow flush ✅ |\\n| Persistence failure | `contextHashBeforeFlush` used in-memory → no re-flush within session ✅ |\\n\\n## Files changed (3 + 1 test)\\n- `src/auto-reply/reply/memory-flush.ts` — new `computeContextHash()` function\\n- `src/auto-reply/reply/agent-runner-memory.ts` — hash check gate + willRetry fix + tail reader\\n- `src/config/sessions/types.ts` — add `memoryFlushContextHash` field to `SessionEntry`\\n- `src/auto-reply/reply/memory-flush.test.ts` — 8 unit tests for `computeContextHash`\\n\\n## Testing\\n- [x] `pnpm build` passes\\n- [x] `pnpm check` passes (lint + format)\\n- [x] `pnpm test` — 811/812 pass (1 pre-existing failure in `process-respawn.test.ts`)\\n- [x] 8 new unit tests for `computeContextHash` (empty input, object content, undefined content, system message filtering, length differentiation, tail behavior)\\n- [x] AI-assisted (OpenClaw agents 李飞飞/陈皮皮/毛豆豆, cross-reviewed, fully tested)\\n\\n## Backward compatibility\\n- `memoryFlushContextHash` undefined → falls back to existing `compactionCount` logic\\n- `memoryFlushCompactionCount` field preserved (not removed)\\n- First flush after upgrade runs normally (hash is empty = allow), subsequent flushes use hash On every subsequent request `resolveSessionModelRef` would return the fallback model, so the configured primary was **never retried** after it recovered.\\n\\n## Root cause\\n\\n`updateSessionStoreAfterAgentRun` unconditionally calls `setSessionRuntimeModel(next, { provider: providerUsed, model: modelUsed })` after every run. When a fallback ran, `providerUsed`/`modelUsed` reflect the fallback, and this gets written to `entry.model` / `entry.modelProvider`. `resolveSessionModelRef` then returns the stored runtime model on every future call, bypassing the configured primary entirely.\\n\\n## Fix\\n\\nAdd an `isFromFallback` parameter to `updateSessionStoreAfterAgentRun`. When true, skip `setSessionRuntimeModel` so the session entry retains no runtime model (or retains its previous primary if one was stored). The WebSocket connection silently stalls behind Docker/VPN proxies (half-open sockets), leaving the web UI frozen with no recovery path.\\n\\nSupersedes #17104, #17132, #17179, #21934 (fixes #21914)\\n\\n### Why it matters\\n\\nDocker is the primary deployment path for self-hosters.
